<div id="review_461571644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461571644" />
    <a title="Beth Bedee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5042872-beth-bedee"><img alt="Beth Bedee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498345228p2/5042872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461571644?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Bedee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Bedee" href="/user/show/5042872-beth-bedee">Beth Bedee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=family-saga">family-saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5042872-beth-bedee?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461571644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16973615750093794743">Another home run by Follett! I absolutely loved this book. I enjoyed it even more than <i>Fall of Giants</i>, and I devoured that. This novel follows the same structure as the first in the Century Trilogy. It picks up in 1933 at Hitlers rise to power. <br/> <br/>Each of the 5 families from the first installment were present, except this time, the story centered around their children, who began the book as teenagers. I felt very connected to the characters in <i>Fall of Giants</i> and thought that it would take me some </span>
  <span id="freeText16973615750093794743" style="display:none">Another home run by Follett! I absolutely loved this book. I enjoyed it even more than <i>Fall of Giants</i>, and I devoured that. This novel follows the same structure as the first in the Century Trilogy. It picks up in 1933 at Hitlers rise to power. <br /> <br />Each of the 5 families from the first installment were present, except this time, the story centered around their children, who began the book as teenagers. I felt very connected to the characters in <i>Fall of Giants</i> and thought that it would take me some time to warm to the next generation. That wasn't so. Follett did an excellent job of "weaning" the reader from the parents. They were very present at the beginning of the novel, but over time, we saw less and less of them, and the next generation took over the plot. Again, time moved swiftly and characters were left for months to years before we heard from them again. I most looked forward to the portions with Daisy and Lloyd, although all the characters had compelling stories. Initially, my least favorite sections were the ones that focused on the Soviet characters. But as the novel progressed,their story was very intriguing as it laid the foundation for the Cold War and book 3.<br /><br />I appreciated that this wasn't just another World War II novel. Much has been written on that topic, even by Follett himself. Instead, I read about topics that haven't seen much coverage: the politics in Germany at Hitler's rise to power, the Fascist movement in England, the Spanish Civil War, Soviet and German espionage, the Pacific theatre, Soviet atrocities during the Fall of Berlin, and the race to create atomic bombs. There were a few war scenes, but on the whole, the novel dealt more with politics. <br /><br />I listened to the audiobook read by John Lee. He was excellent. I was most impressed with his ability to capture the characters through their different accents and dialects. I'd highly recommend listening to this one.<br /><br />I was sorry to see the book end. I absolutely can't wait until September 2014 for <i>Edge of Eternity</i>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16973615750093794743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6700841596696829426">Of course, you must read FALL OF GIANTS first....it's just now out in mass paperback, I noticed. I bought the hardcover, some time back,and actually carried it to the Kansas City area to read it,and didn't start it.....months later I finally did,and loved it....I grew fond of the characters,and felt like they were my personal friends.... the 2nd book in this trilogy? I felt the same. I felt the pain, the joy, the love, the anguish of all that the characters were going through..... WW I and WW II</span>
  <span id="freeText6700841596696829426" style="display:none">Of course, you must read FALL OF GIANTS first....it's just now out in mass paperback, I noticed. I bought the hardcover, some time back,and actually carried it to the Kansas City area to read it,and didn't start it.....months later I finally did,and loved it....I grew fond of the characters,and felt like they were my personal friends.... the 2nd book in this trilogy? I felt the same. I felt the pain, the joy, the love, the anguish of all that the characters were going through..... WW I and WW II ,and all the drama focused around their lives. I felt like I was a huge part of their lives........ What a sign of a truly impressive novel,and the richness of it's writing! I just now finished WINTER,and I am ready for book number 3 now!<br /><br /><br />To me, all of the above comments tell me about what a great writer Follett is and what super books these are......I can assure you that you won't be disappointed,and don't let the length of the novels deter you....it reads quick,and a lot of things happen to these characters. Follett spends a lot of time researching his facts,and in my estimation he is the king of historical fiction these days.....<br /><br /><br />Pick up the first book,and be prepared to be riveted!!<br /><br />Then read book # 2. I am anxious to hear of a date for release of the final installment!</span>

<div id="review_541292290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541292290" />
    <a title="Peterspepper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4954571-peterspepper"><img alt="Peterspepper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297288831p2/4954571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/541292290?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peterspepper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peterspepper" href="/user/show/4954571-peterspepper">Peterspepper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer541292290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16386705946610268451">I'm more of a review reader than a review writer here on GoodReads. However, I felt moved to say a few words regarding the quality, or lack thereof, pertinent to Ken Follett's Winter of the World. <br/><br/>I've read two previous books by Ken Follett, the cathedral building series (Pillars of the Earth and ???). I enjoyed them both. So, I decided to pick up Winter of the World (book two in the latest series) because I'm a huge fan of anything historical concerning WWII. And typically, historical fiction i</span>
  <span id="freeText16386705946610268451" style="display:none">I'm more of a review reader than a review writer here on GoodReads. However, I felt moved to say a few words regarding the quality, or lack thereof, pertinent to Ken Follett's Winter of the World. <br /><br />I've read two previous books by Ken Follett, the cathedral building series (Pillars of the Earth and ???). I enjoyed them both. So, I decided to pick up Winter of the World (book two in the latest series) because I'm a huge fan of anything historical concerning WWII. And typically, historical fiction is what Follett does best! However, IMHO, I'm afraid he seriously missed the mark on this venture. <br /><br />I found his references to historical fact to be extremely dull, seriously lacking in the rich dimension that was the reality of our world at that time. So interesting, yet depicted so flatly. What a lost opportunity. Additionally, his characters evoked almost no emotion from me and their dialog was so exceptionally boring as to be almost child-like! <br /><br />I had intended to go back and read the first book in this series, covering WWI, but I believe I'll pass. And, I'm VERY pleased I decided not to invest in the $20+ cost of purchasing the ebook! I suggest borrowing it from your local library should you decide to wade into this quagmire of a book! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16386705946610268451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Book Maven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Book Maven" href="/user/show/47212-the-book-maven">The Book Maven</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464830126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2852299450070520868">There are many things that I can say about Ken Follett and the second book in his <i>Century</i> trilogy--and remarkably, just about everything I have to say is good!<br/><br/>-First, Ken Follett's books are where history, soap opera, good storytelling, and statistically improbably coincidence meet.<br/><br/>-Second, Ken Follett is an unlikely combination of Edward Rutherfurd and Danielle Steel.<br/><br/>-Third, if you have a person who likes to read, but hates history, this would be the kind of book to give him.<br/><br/>-My issue with leng</span>
  <span id="freeText2852299450070520868" style="display:none">There are many things that I can say about Ken Follett and the second book in his <i>Century</i> trilogy--and remarkably, just about everything I have to say is good!<br /><br />-First, Ken Follett's books are where history, soap opera, good storytelling, and statistically improbably coincidence meet.<br /><br />-Second, Ken Follett is an unlikely combination of Edward Rutherfurd and Danielle Steel.<br /><br />-Third, if you have a person who likes to read, but hates history, this would be the kind of book to give him.<br /><br />-My issue with lengthy, multi-volume tomes like this is that a lot of times, I forget characters, connections, and events between publications. Follett skillfully makes everything clear without ever making you feel as though stuff is being rehashed.<br /><br />-Fourth, last, and most important (and complimentary): even to this day, we often wonder about the collective insanity that gripped Europe (specifically, Germany, France, Italy, etc.) when they embraced National Socialism. Follett does an outstanding, let me repeat, <i>
  <b>OUTSTANDING</b>
</i> job of portraying (without preaching) how good, regular Germans could be utterly oppressed and bullied into fearfully remaining silent as Hitler and the Nazis destroyed their country. What Follett's books lack in profundity, they make up for in empathy and an accurate historical perspective.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2852299450070520868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_428994848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428994848" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1029790-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208460948p2/1029790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/428994848?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/1029790-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428994848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10825504320883155488">Let me begin by saying that I could not put this book, or rather my ipad, down until I read the whole thing. It took me two days to get through it and I was so excited over it that I couldn't read it fast enough. As historical novels go, I found it very entertaining and it seemed plausible that all of these characters could experience the events Follett depicted. However, I couldn't help but compare Winter of the World with Herman Wouk's utterly amazing The Winds of War and its sequel, War and R</span>
  <span id="freeText10825504320883155488" style="display:none">Let me begin by saying that I could not put this book, or rather my ipad, down until I read the whole thing. It took me two days to get through it and I was so excited over it that I couldn't read it fast enough. As historical novels go, I found it very entertaining and it seemed plausible that all of these characters could experience the events Follett depicted. However, I couldn't help but compare Winter of the World with Herman Wouk's utterly amazing The Winds of War and its sequel, War and Remembrance. In scope and volume, Winter of the World cannot compare to Wouk's works. Wouk's two novels cover the events of World War II from 1939 to 1945, while Winter of the World covers 1933 to 1949 in one volume. Wouk covered almost every major event of World War II, and included a huge amount of information about the Holocaust. Follett does not cover a quarter of the information that Wouk covered and the Holocaust is only mentioned by the major characters; no major character experiences the Holocaust. I love both The Winds of War and War and Remembrance and read them every few years, but despite the fact that they are more historically accurate, contain much more information about the war, and explain the major battles and campaigns of the war in greater detail, I think that Winter of the World is a more entertaining read. Winter of the World reminded me of a great spy novel, with a great deal of time spent on clandestine activities and just the right amount of suspense. Also, the characters are written in a way that I felt very invested in them. He spent just enough time on each character's arc that I cared about what happened to them but not so long that I wanted to skip ahead to see what happened next in another character's arc. I must confess that I skip around in Wouk's books to my favorite characters. I did not feel the impetus to do that here because I found each arc very interesting. Winter of the World was more of a novel set in a historical period while Wouk's novels are more history books with fictional characters. I highly recommend this novel and am looking forward very much to the final book in the trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10825504320883155488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_420033162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420033162" />
    <a title="happy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9369133-happy"><img alt="happy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414901547p2/9369133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420033162?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="happy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="happy" href="/user/show/9369133-happy">happy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9369133-happy?shelf=fiction-historical">fiction-historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420033162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6503769531726242098">I don’t think this was Mr. Follett’s best effort. While it is entertaining, it just didn’t suck me in like many of his other works including the first volume of this trilogy.<br/><br/>This volume is set from 1933-1949 and covers the Hitler’s seizure of power – the politics of 1930 England (the Labour/socialist Party vs the Tories/industrialist), the Spanish Civil war, the Battle of Britain from the pov of the people on the ground in London, espionage - both by both the Soviets and the Brits, development o</span>
  <span id="freeText6503769531726242098" style="display:none">I don’t think this was Mr. Follett’s best effort. While it is entertaining, it just didn’t suck me in like many of his other works including the first volume of this trilogy.<br /><br />This volume is set from 1933-1949 and covers the Hitler’s seizure of power – the politics of 1930 England (the Labour/socialist Party vs the Tories/industrialist), the Spanish Civil war, the Battle of Britain from the pov of the people on the ground in London, espionage - both by both the Soviets and the Brits, development of the atomic bomb and just about every important conference or event that happened in that time frame.<br /><br />For a book largely set in WW II there is surprising little combat ( some in Spain, Pearl Harbor, Midway and a brief scene in Normandy post invasion ).<br /><br />The five families that were introduced in Fall of Giants return in the next generation, with the characters from the first book providing mainly supporting roles.<br /><br />One problem I had with this book is the coincidences that happen to put his characters in a position to observe the great events of the day. For example he has one of the families, civilians no less, in the middle of Pearl Harbor heading for breakfast on the Arizona as the attack begins, fairly unbelievable imo.<br /><br />Another gripe I had with the book and with the first also to some extent is that Follett presents the Industrialist/Conservatives as the bad guys. I can’t think of one conservative character who would be considered a good guy in this novel. All the good guys are socialists. I think it is a wee bit heavy handed on Follett’s part.<br /><br />All that said it was an enjoyable read, fairly quick read and I will read the final volume when it is released.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6503769531726242098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nIPjOinNTTp28nGqGWiLdaaOeYYgmaxSIYSFCoHwFsA+r4YCfeTU23TJjodcmhnvNlAZT+70ymIoyk7UztrqTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y2fvQpmRcwDu0qWlE0Vsm3Cuxf/u/s5eAsK4vUMjSG9pS4p6zbjq4ezpWohWt/4B4HClNiCTqG4LjHNjDAm04w==')})
  }

The novel Edge of Eternity narrates the fictional stories of the descendants of <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7324667891321972699\" style=\"display:none\">Edge of Eternity: by Ken Follett (The Century Trilogy, Book 3) | Summary &amp; Analysis by Book*Sense  This is a Summary &amp; Analysis of Ken Follett’s novel, Edge of Eternity. The novel Edge of Eternity narrates the fictional stories of the descendants of Ma Peshkov, their families and their associates in the United States, the United Kingdom, divided Germany and the USSR through the decades of the all-too-real existence of the Berlin Wall and the thrust of the United States Civil Rights movement and into the generation after. Several of them—notably George Jakes, Rebecca Held and Dimka Dvorkin—find themselves in positions of political power and influence near, but not at, the top of their countries’ governments across several decades. The ten-part narrative attends closely to them, as well as to their more artistically inclined cousins as they negotiate the sociopolitical turmoil of the 1960s, 1970s and 1980s, with a brief epilogue set in 2008.  Ken Follett’s sweeping Century Trilogy concludes with Edge of Eternity. It is a substantial read covering more than fifty years of recent history offering a detailed and authentic account of world events as they could have been seen by those in positions near those in power which will be looked at in this companion. As a work of historical fiction, it is based upon and treats real events, but it does so from the peripheries that, still closer to the action than many or most of the readers could be, lie outside those already so thoroughly known to history and almost mythologized in multiple retellings. Thus, Follett’s Edge of Eternity presents an unusual, and ultimately more compelling, perspective on the events that shaped the last third of the twentieth century and whose effects are still being felt a generation afterwards. Nevertheless, Edge of Eternity has its shortcomings. Apoyándose en el oscuro poema épico de Dante, Langdon, en una carrera contrarreloj, busca respuestas y personas de confianza antes de que el mundo cambie irrevocablemente.Ángeles y demonios Robert Langdon es convocado a un centro de investigación suizo para analizar un misterioso símbolo marcado a fuego en el pecho de un físico asesinado. Los peores temores de Langdon se confirman cuando los illuminati anuncian que han escondido una bomba en el corazón de la Ciudad del Vaticano. Con la cuenta atrás en marcha, Langdon viaja a Roma para unir fuerzas con Vittoria Vetra, una científica bella y misteriosa. Los dos se embarcarán en una carrera contrarreloj en una búsqueda desesperada por los rincones menos conocidos del Vaticano. El arma más poderosa creada por el hombre, una organización secreta sedienta de venganza... y apenas unas horas para evitar el desastre. Aquel niño recibió el nombre de su progenitor, Publio Cornelio Escipión, quien fuera cónsul de Roma durante el primer año de aquella guerra. Las hazañas del hijo del cónsul alcanzaron tal magnitud que el pueblo le concedió un sobrenombre especial, un apelativo referente a uno de los territorios que conquistó: Africanus. Africanus, el hi­jo del cónsul narra con una prosa ágil y directa el tormentoso y a la vez fascinante mundo de la juventud de Publio Cornelio Escipión, el Africano. Pero ¿qué ocurrió para que Roma aceptara por emperador a alguien no nacido en la misma Roma, sino a alguien proveniente de las lejanas y agrestes tierras de Hispania? Hernando busca libertad y respeto, pero se encuentra con la brutalidad de unos y otros. También descubre el amor, en la persona de la valerosa Fátima, la de los hermosos ojos negros.Tras la derrota de la insurrección, Hernando es deportado a la ciudad de Córdoba, la hermosa ciudad que aún conserva el legado de su pasado árabe. En ella Hernando intenta comenzar una nueva vida, que será una nueva etapa en la lucha por la tolerancia y la concordia entre las dos culturas.El autor de La catedral del mar vuelve con una trepidante novela con las mismas claves que llevaron al éxito a la primera: fidelidad histórica entrecruzada con un conmovedor relato de amor y odio, de ilusiones perdidas y esperanzas que dan sentido a la vida       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3447.Ken_Follett">About Ken Follett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9565359637412724860">Ken Follett is one of the world’s most successful authors. Over 170 million copies of the 36 books he has written have been sold in over 80 countries and in 33 languages.<br/><br/>Born on June 5th, 1949 in Cardiff, Wales, the son of a tax inspector, Ken was educated at state schools and went on to graduate from University College, London, with an Honours degree in Philosophy – later to be made a Fellow of t</span>
  <span id="freeText9565359637412724860" style="display:none">Ken Follett is one of the world’s most successful authors. Over 170 million copies of the 36 books he has written have been sold in over 80 countries and in 33 languages.<br /><br />Born on June 5th, 1949 in Cardiff, Wales, the son of a tax inspector, Ken was educated at state schools and went on to graduate from University College, London, with an Honours degree in Philosophy – later to be made a Fellow of the College in 1995.<br /><br />He started his career as a reporter, first with his hometown newspaper the South Wales Echo and then with the London Evening News. Subsequently, he worked for a small London publishing house, Everest Books, eventually becoming Deputy Managing Director.<br /><br />Ken’s first major success came with the publication of Eye of the Needle in 1978. A World War II thriller set in England, this book earned him the 1979 Edgar Award for Best Novel from the Mystery Writers of America. It remains one of Ken’s most popular books.<br /><br />In 1989, Ken’s epic novel about the building of a medieval cathedral, The Pillars of the Earth, was published. It reached number one on best-seller lists everywhere and was turned into a major television series produced by Ridley Scott, which aired in 2010. World Without End, the sequel to The Pillars of the Earth, proved equally popular when it was published in 2007.<br /><br />Ken’s new book, The Evening and the Morning, will be published in September 2020. It is a prequel to The Pillars of the Earth and is set around the year 1,000, when Kingsbridge was an Anglo-Saxon settlement threatened by Viking invaders.<br /><br />Ken has been active in numerous literacy charities and was president of Dyslexia Action for ten years. He was chair of the National Year of Reading, a joint initiative between government and businesses. He is also active in many Stevenage charities and is President of the Stevenage Community Trust and Patron of Home-Start Hertfordshire.<br /><br />Ken, who loves music almost as much as he loves books, is an enthusiastic bass guitar player. He lives in Stevenage, Hertfordshire, with his wife Barbara, the former Labour Member of Parliament for Stevenage. Between them they have five children, six grandchildren and two Labradors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9565359637412724860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
